</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Formerly of</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/GothBoiClique" title="GothBoiClique">GothBoiClique</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://lilpeep.com">lilpeep<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Gustav Elijah Åhr</b> (<small>Swedish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="sv-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Swedish" title="Help:IPA/Swedish">[ˈoːr]</a></span>; November 1, 1996 – November 15, 2017), known professionally as <b>Lil Peep,</b> was a Swedish-American rapper and singer-songwriter.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Emo_rap" title="Emo rap">emo rap</a> collective <a href="/wiki/GothBoiClique" title="GothBoiClique">GothBoiClique</a>. Helping pioneer an <a href="/wiki/Emo_revival" title="Emo revival">emo revival</a>-style of <a href="/wiki/Rapping" title="Rapping">rap</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> music, Lil Peep has been credited as a leading figure of the mid–late 2010s emo rap scene and came to be an inspiration to outcasts and <a href="/wiki/Youth_subculture" title="Youth subculture">youth subcultures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Allentown,_Pennsylvania" title="Allentown, Pennsylvania">Allentown, Pennsylvania</a>, to an American mother and a Swedish father and raised on <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>, Åhr started releasing music on <a href="/wiki/SoundCloud" title="SoundCloud">SoundCloud</a> in 2013 under the name "Trap Goose",<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> later changing his artist name to Lil Peep because his mother had called him "Peep" since he was a baby.<sup id="cite_ref-:13222_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13222-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He soon became popular on the platform with the release of his 2015 single "Star Shopping", and his popularity grew further with his release of mixtapes <i><a href="/wiki/Lil_Peep;_Part_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Lil Peep; Part One">Lil Peep; Part One</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Live_Forever_(Lil_Peep_mixtape)" title="Live Forever (Lil Peep mixtape)"><i>Live Forever</i></a> later that year. In 2016, Lil Peep released his widely acclaimed mixtapes <a href="/wiki/Crybaby_(Lil_Peep_mixtape)" title="Crybaby (Lil Peep mixtape)"><i>Crybaby</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Hellboy_(Lil_Peep_mixtape)" title="Hellboy (Lil Peep mixtape)"><i>Hellboy</i></a>, along with many other projects including <a href="/wiki/Lil_Peep_discography" title="Lil Peep discography"><i>California Girls</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Lil_Peep_discography" title="Lil Peep discography"><i>Vertigo</i></a>.
</p><p>Lil Peep's first live performance was February 12, 2016, in <a href="/wiki/Tucson,_Arizona" title="Tucson, Arizona">Tucson</a> as member of Schemaposse. Later that year, he toured briefly with <a href="/wiki/Fat_Nick" title="Fat Nick">Fat Nick</a>, Mikey The Magician, and <a href="/wiki/Smokepurpp" title="Smokepurpp">Smokepurpp</a>. In the spring of 2017, Lil Peep embarked on his first solo tour, performing to packed venues in three Russian cities, making his way across western Europe, and then across the United States. Soon after the tour Lil Peep moved to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, where he recorded his EP <i><a href="/wiki/Goth_Angel_Sinner" title="Goth Angel Sinner">Goth Angel Sinner</a></i>, and in August he released his debut studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Come_Over_When_You%27re_Sober,_Pt._1" title="Come Over When You&#39;re Sober, Pt. 1">Come Over When You're Sober, Pt. 1</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While his mixtapes explored <a href="/wiki/Emo" title="Emo">emo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trap_music" title="Trap music">trap</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lo-fi_music" title="Lo-fi music">lo-fi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative rock</a>, his debut album was a transition into <a href="/wiki/Pop_punk" class="mw-redirect" title="Pop punk">pop punk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rap_rock" title="Rap rock">rap rock</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> His second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Come_Over_When_You%27re_Sober,_Pt._2" title="Come Over When You&#39;re Sober, Pt. 2">Come Over When You're Sober, Pt. 2</a></i>, was released in 2018 and debuted at number four on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BB2002_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BB2002-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Documentary_film" title="Documentary film">documentary film</a> about him, <i><a href="/wiki/Everybody%27s_Everything_(film)" title="Everybody&#39;s Everything (film)">Everybody's Everything</a></i>, was released in 2019.
</p><p>On November 15, 2017, two weeks after his 21st birthday, Lil Peep died on his tour bus before a scheduled performance in Tucson, his second to last scheduled show on a 33-date tour of the United States. The <a href="/wiki/Pima_County,_Arizona" title="Pima County, Arizona">Pima County</a> medical examiner's office, which conducted <a href="/wiki/Toxicology" title="Toxicology">toxicology</a> tests on Lil Peep, ruled his cause of death an accidental overdose of <a href="/wiki/Fentanyl" title="Fentanyl">fentanyl</a>, a powerful <a href="/wiki/Opioid" title="Opioid">opioid</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alprazolam" title="Alprazolam">Xanax</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine" title="Benzodiazepine">benzodiazepine</a> <a href="/wiki/Sedative" title="Sedative">sedative</a>. His death was observed as a great loss to 21st-century music. "He could have been his generation's <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain" title="Kurt Cobain">Kurt Cobain</a>", a <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> profile stated.<sup id="cite_ref-deathofficial2_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deathofficial2-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone.com_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone.com-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Peep&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Gustav Elijah Åhr was born on November 1, 1996, in <a href="/wiki/Allentown,_Pennsylvania" title="Allentown, Pennsylvania">Allentown, Pennsylvania</a>, the second child of first grade teacher Liza Womack. His maternal grandfather is <a href="/wiki/John_Womack" title="John Womack">John Womack</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> professor of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin American</a> history and economics and a specialist on <a href="/wiki/Emiliano_Zapata" title="Emiliano Zapata">Emiliano Zapata</a>, a leader of the early 20th century <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He moved to <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach,_New_York" title="Long Beach, New York">Long Beach, New York</a> on <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a> before his fifth birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He had one sibling, Karl "Oskar" Åhr.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> His parents were both <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a> graduates.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> His mother's family is from <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a> and his father is Swedish.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-V_Magazine_2019_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-V_Magazine_2019-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Åhr's Swedish citizenship was granted to him through his father in accordance with Swedish law which states that Swedish citizenship is granted automatically at birth to anyone with at least one Swedish parent.<sup id="cite_ref-Swedish_Migration_Agency_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swedish_Migration_Agency-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Åhr's parents separated in 2012 when he was 15. He began experiencing <a href="/wiki/Anxiety" title="Anxiety">anxiety</a> around age 16 and, according to his mother, self-medicated with <a href="/wiki/Marijuana" class="mw-redirect" title="Marijuana">marijuana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alprazolam" title="Alprazolam">Xanax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone.com_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone.com-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Lil Peep had a close relationship with his mother, going so far as to tattoo her initials and birthday on his arm as his first tattoo at the age of 14.<sup id="cite_ref-:13222_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13222-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Following his parents' split, he moved with his mother and older brother to Long Beach, New York, where he would eventually record "<a href="/wiki/Lil_Peep;_Part_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Lil Peep; Part One">Lil Peep; Part One</a>", Feelz, Vertigo, most of "California Girls," "Garden," "In the Bedroom I Confess," "Mall Music," "Romeo's Regrets," and several tracks that were released as singles, including "Star Shopping".
</p><p>Åhr attended Lindell Elementary School, located just across the street from his mother's apartment in Long Beach. Just a few days into Åhr's kindergarten year, the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> took place with smoke plumes clearly visible from Åhr's kindergarten classroom. In third grade, Åhr was placed in Long Beach's gifted and talented program. Later, in middle school, he was placed in accelerated classes. He played the trombone and tuba<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and expressed an interest in music and fashion from a young age. Åhr attended <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach_High_School_(New_York)" title="Long Beach High School (New York)">Long Beach High School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lido_Beach,_New_York" title="Lido Beach, New York">Lido Beach</a>, New York, which was directly impacted by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">Hurricane Sandy</a> in 2012 and caused the school to close for a few weeks. When the school reopened, the faculty and administrators were more relaxed on the students, leading Åhr to enjoy his junior year of high school significantly more than the rest.
</p><p>When Åhr returned to school the following year as a senior, there was a new administration that was unfamiliar with the student body and culture. An exhausted Åhr was ready to drop out, but was assisted by a teacher named Maria Hartmann to finish school. With the help of two other teachers whom Åhr knew and trusted, Åhr finished high school by completing his last two necessary courses, English and Social Studies. He graduated six months early in January 2014.
</p><p>Later that January, Åhr was accepted into <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_at_Old_Westbury" title="State University of New York at Old Westbury">SUNY Old Westbury</a> on Long Island, but declined to attend and instead enrolled as an out of state student at <a href="/wiki/Glendale_Community_College_(California)" title="Glendale Community College (California)">Glendale Community College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena, California</a>. There, he was able to enroll in one class with a middle school friend, who ultimately dropped out. After his first semester at Glendale Community College, Åhr decided to drop out and instead enrolled at <a href="/wiki/Nassau_Community_College" title="Nassau Community College">Nassau Community College</a> on Long Island. By the fall of 2015, Åhr was taking four classes online (two business classes, one criminal justice class, and one art history class) in which he earned three A's and one B.
</p><p>During Åhr's only full-time semester at Nassau Community College, he made the dean's list. However, instead of enrolling in a second term, Åhr decided to drop out and begin performing with Schemaposse. By the end of 2015 he had already completed a large body of work in his bedroom while attending school full-time.<sup id="cite_ref-Official_Website_of_the_Estate_of_Gustav_Ahr_/_Lil_Peep_2021_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Website_of_the_Estate_of_Gustav_Ahr_/_Lil_Peep_2021-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:22_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:22-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:10_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the age of 18, Åhr got his first face tattoo, a broken heart below his left eye, as a sign of commitment to avoiding a straight life. "A tattoo on your face is gonna stop you from getting a lot of jobs," he would later say.<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone.com_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone.com-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> He returned to <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> to pursue a career in music under the stage name Lil Peep in February 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> He moved to Los Angeles, he later explained, because living on Long Island depressed him.<sup id="cite_ref-:22_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:22-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Peep&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lil_Peep_%26_Fat_Nick,_Texas,_November_2016.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Lil_Peep_%26_Fat_Nick%2C_Texas%2C_November_2016.jpg/220px-Lil_Peep_%26_Fat_Nick%2C_Texas%2C_November_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="101" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Lil_Peep_%26_Fat_Nick%2C_Texas%2C_November_2016.jpg/330px-Lil_Peep_%26_Fat_Nick%2C_Texas%2C_November_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Lil_Peep_%26_Fat_Nick%2C_Texas%2C_November_2016.jpg/440px-Lil_Peep_%26_Fat_Nick%2C_Texas%2C_November_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="589" /></a><figcaption>Lil Peep (left) performing with <a href="/wiki/Fat_Nick" title="Fat Nick">Fat Nick</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio" title="San Antonio">San Antonio</a> in November 2016</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lil_Peep,_Holland,_October_2017.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Lil_Peep%2C_Holland%2C_October_2017.png/220px-Lil_Peep%2C_Holland%2C_October_2017.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="113" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Lil_Peep%2C_Holland%2C_October_2017.png/330px-Lil_Peep%2C_Holland%2C_October_2017.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Lil_Peep%2C_Holland%2C_October_2017.png/440px-Lil_Peep%2C_Holland%2C_October_2017.png 2x" data-file-width="899" data-file-height="462" /></a><figcaption>Lil Peep performing in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> in October 2017<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lil_Peep,_Toronto,_2017.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Lil_Peep%2C_Toronto%2C_2017.png/220px-Lil_Peep%2C_Toronto%2C_2017.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="378" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ce/Lil_Peep%2C_Toronto%2C_2017.png 1.5x" data-file-width="321" data-file-height="551" /></a><figcaption>Lil Peep performing in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> in October 2017</figcaption></figure>
<p>When Lil Peep was a teenager, he was self-described as a loner who made most of his friends online. Inspired by underground acts like <a href="/wiki/Seshollowaterboyz" class="mw-redirect" title="Seshollowaterboyz">Seshollowaterboyz</a> and <a href="/wiki/ILoveMakonnen" title="ILoveMakonnen">iLoveMakonnen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-HAM_ON_EVERYTHING_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HAM_ON_EVERYTHING-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Peep made music while residing on Long Island<sup id="cite_ref-For_Lil_Peep_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-For_Lil_Peep-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> under the pseudonym "Trap Goose"<sup id="cite_ref-:10_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and lived temporarily with childhood friend Brennan Savage until both decided to move to Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-:23_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:23-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Los Angeles, Lil Peep initially lived in <a href="/wiki/Skid_Row,_Los_Angeles" title="Skid Row, Los Angeles">Skid Row</a> and dipped in and out of homelessness,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> staying at Savage's apartment while Savage pursued a degree. The two eventually went separate ways,<sup id="cite_ref-:23_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:23-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> and Peep met Atlanta rapper and producer JGRXXN, Florida rapper <a href="/wiki/Ghostemane" title="Ghostemane">Ghostemane</a> and Houston rapper <a href="/wiki/Craig_Xen" title="Craig Xen">Craig Xen</a>, living with them while forming the collective Schemaposse.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> He originally met Craig Xen online and was introduced to JGRXXN, who needed a singer.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Lil Peep also attended <a href="/wiki/Glendale_Community_College_(California)" title="Glendale Community College (California)">Glendale Community College</a> during his first year in Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, Peep released his first extended play, <i>Feelz.</i> This was followed by his debut mixtape <i>Lil Peep; Part One</i>, which generated 4,000 plays in its first week. Shortly thereafter, he released a follow-up mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Live_Forever_(Lil_Peep_mixtape)" title="Live Forever (Lil Peep mixtape)">Live Forever</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lil Peep began to grow in popularity in the fall of 2015, garnered by the popularity of songs such as "Star Shopping" (later released as a single posthumously)<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> making waves in underground hip-hop circles.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Lil Peep's popularity continued to rise after the release of the song "Beamer Boy", which led to him performing live for the first time with the rest of Schemaposse in February 2016 in Tucson, Arizona.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In April, Schemaposse broke up and Lil Peep was no longer associated with a collective, though they remained on good terms.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after Schemaposse's breakup, Peep began to associate with Los Angeles-based rap collective <a href="/wiki/GothBoiClique" title="GothBoiClique">GothBoiClique</a>, featuring members of the group on his full-length mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Crybaby_(Lil_Peep_mixtape)" title="Crybaby (Lil Peep mixtape)">Crybaby</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The group shared a squat in Skid Row with Peep and often shared beds.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> <i>Crybaby</i> was recorded over the span of one month and was completed hours before its original release on SoundCloud in June 2016. Peep completed a majority of the mixing and mastering himself.<sup id="cite_ref-HAM_ON_EVERYTHING_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HAM_ON_EVERYTHING-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In August, <a href="/wiki/First_Access_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="First Access Entertainment">First Access Entertainment</a> (FAE) partnered with Lil Peep on a joint venture to invest in and advise him on his career.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2016, Lil Peep released his fourth and final solo mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Hellboy_(Lil_Peep_mixtape)" title="Hellboy (Lil Peep mixtape)">Hellboy</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Songs from <i>Hellboy</i> such as "Girls" and "OMFG" received millions of views and plays on <a href="/wiki/SoundCloud" title="SoundCloud">SoundCloud</a> and YouTube.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> <i>Hellboy</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> success led to Peep's first solo tour across the United States and Europe in the spring of 2017, which included performances in Russia and the UK for the first time in his career.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In May 2017, the band <a href="/wiki/Mineral_(band)" title="Mineral (band)">Mineral</a> accused Peep of <a href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement" title="Copyright infringement">copyright infringement</a> for including an unlicensed and uncredited <a href="/wiki/Sampling_(music)" title="Sampling (music)">sample</a> of their song "LoveLetterTypewriter" on his track "Hollywood Dreaming". Peep said that he was only trying to "show some love" with the sample.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Soon after the tour was completed, Peep emigrated to London, England, during a disentanglement with Gothboiclique. There he began to associate with figures such as Atlanta rapper iLoveMakonnen and longtime friend Bexey, and recorded <i><a href="/wiki/Come_Over_When_You%27re_Sober,_Pt._1" title="Come Over When You&#39;re Sober, Pt. 1">Come Over When You're Sober, Pt. 1</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Come_Over_When_You%27re_Sober,_Pt._2" title="Come Over When You&#39;re Sober, Pt. 2">Come Over When You're Sober, Pt. 2</a></i>, the EP <i><a href="/wiki/Goth_Angel_Sinner" title="Goth Angel Sinner">Goth Angel Sinner</a></i> and an unreleased collaborative project with iLoveMakonnen.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:24_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:24-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Peep released his debut studio album, <i>Come Over When You're Sober, Pt. 1</i>, on August 15, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Shortly thereafter he embarked on his second world tour, beginning in the UK in September<sup id="cite_ref-:25_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:25-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and moving to Germany before finishing in the United States in November, which was cut short by his death.<sup id="cite_ref-:26_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:26-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Posthumous_releases">Posthumous releases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Peep&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Posthumous releases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After his death, Lil Peep's fanbase and popularity grew quickly, resulting in a significant increase in sales and streams of his music.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The single "<a href="/wiki/Awful_Things" title="Awful Things">Awful Things</a>" from <i>Come Over When You're Sober, Part One</i> charted, becoming his first entry on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 at number 79.
</p><p>Due to Peep's prolific work rate, a number of songs and projects were completed prior to his death. The first official posthumous release arrived within 24 hours of his death, as Wiggy, a director of many of Peep's music videos, released the official video for the then-unreleased song "16 Lines".<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> On January 12, 2018, <a href="/wiki/Marshmello" title="Marshmello">Marshmello</a> officially released a collaboration titled "<a href="/wiki/Spotlight_(Marshmello_and_Lil_Peep_song)" title="Spotlight (Marshmello and Lil Peep song)">Spotlight</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The video for "Spotlight" was released on February 12, 2018. On January 15, 2018, rapper <a href="/wiki/Juicy_J" title="Juicy J">Juicy J</a> released the song "Got 'Em Like", which featured Lil Peep and <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On January 27, 2018, SoundCloud rapper Teddy released a song collaboration with Lil Peep, "Dreams &amp; Nightmares".<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2018, Peep's music archive was acquired by <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a>. On May 13, 2018, a posthumous single, "<a href="/wiki/4_Gold_Chains" title="4 Gold Chains">4 Gold Chains</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Clams_Casino_(musician)" title="Clams Casino (musician)">Clams Casino</a>, was released as well as a music video.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> A collaboration album between Peep and rapper <a href="/wiki/ILoveMakonnen" title="ILoveMakonnen">iLoveMakonnen</a> is expected to be released on Makonnen's label Warner Bros.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> On August 17, 2018, Makonnen announced a new Lil Peep single, "<a href="/wiki/Falling_Down_(Lil_Peep_and_XXXTentacion_song)" title="Falling Down (Lil Peep and XXXTentacion song)">Falling Down</a>", a reworking of "Sunlight on Your Skin" that he recorded with Peep in the fall of 2017 in London. The new version features recently deceased rapper <a href="/wiki/XXXTentacion" title="XXXTentacion">XXXTentacion</a>, who recorded his verses following Peep's death.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The creation of the single was condemned by some surviving members of GothBoiClique, who said there had been unresolved conflict between the two artists stemming from latter's alleged <a href="/wiki/XXXTentacion#Legal_issues" title="XXXTentacion">history of violence</a> towards women.<sup id="cite_ref-Daramola_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daramola-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> This was disputed by other close friends of Lil Peep.<sup id="cite_ref-hotnewhiphop.com_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hotnewhiphop.com-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> "Falling Down" was released on September 19, 2018, and peaked at number 13 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup id="cite_ref-fallingdown_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fallingdown-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The original "Sunlight on Your Skin" was released on September 27, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 14, 2018, Lil Peep's estate revealed that his first posthumous project, <i>Come Over When You're Sober, Pt. 2</i>, was finished in September 2018 and Lil Peep's executive producer for the project, Smokeasac, confirmed that it was just awaiting approval from Peep's family.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> On October 17, 2018, Lil Peep's estate confirmed that the lead single from <i>Come Over When You're Sober, Pt. 2,</i> "Cry Alone", would be released on October 18, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> <i>Come Over When You're Sober, Pt. 2</i> was released on November 9, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-:16222_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:16222-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> On November 1, 2018, the second single from the album, "Runaway", was officially released.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> On November 7, 2018, the third single, "Life is Beautiful"—a remix of the track "Life" from the <i>Feelz</i> EP—was released.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Come Over When You're Sober, Pt. 2</i> debuted at number four on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 with 81,000 <a href="/wiki/Album-equivalent_unit" title="Album-equivalent unit">album-equivalent units</a> (including 43,000 pure album sales), making it Lil Peep's first US top 10 album.<sup id="cite_ref-BB2002_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BB2002-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 31, 2019, the first single from the upcoming collaboration album with iLoveMakonnen, "<a href="/wiki/I%27ve_Been_Waiting_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="I&#39;ve Been Waiting (song)">I've Been Waiting</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Fall_Out_Boy" title="Fall Out Boy">Fall Out Boy</a>, was released.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The song was originally a demo by ILoveMakonnen; Peep then performed on it, spawning a partnership that created up to 20 songs. Fall Out Boy was added to the song after Peep's death.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 10, 2019, the documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Everybody%27s_Everything_(film)" title="Everybody&#39;s Everything (film)">Everybody's Everything</a></i>, which chronicles Lil Peep's life, premiered at the <a href="/wiki/SXSW_Film_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="SXSW Film Festival">SXSW Film Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> On November 1, 2019, the estate announced the release of the <a href="/wiki/Everybody%27s_Everything_(album)" title="Everybody&#39;s Everything (album)">soundtrack</a> to the documentary, which features both previously released and unreleased tracks.
</p><p>In April 2019, "Gym Class" and "Star Shopping", two Lil Peep singles that were originally released in March 2016 and August 2015 respectively, were re-released onto all streaming platforms by the Lil Peep estate.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The 2016 EP <i>Vertigo</i> was subsequently released by the estate to streaming platforms on March 5, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The Peep estate officially released the <i>Crybaby</i> mixtape with most samples cleared to all streaming platforms on June 10, 2020, to coincide with the four-year anniversary of the original release.<sup id="cite_ref-:11_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:11-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The track "falling 4 me" was missing as it could not be cleared with Radiohead.<sup id="cite_ref-:11_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:11-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The estate released the <i><a href="/wiki/Hellboy_(Lil_Peep_mixtape)" title="Hellboy (Lil Peep mixtape)">Hellboy</a></i> mixtape with most samples cleared on September 25, 2020, the fourth anniversary of its original release.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The song "drive by" was reproduced due to sample clearance issues.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 26, 2021, the estate announced that the <i>California Girls</i> EP was to be re-released.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> It was released on January 29, 2021, with a music video for the song "lil kennedy".<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Later, on June 30, 2021, the estate announced the re-release of the Lil Peep and Lil Tracy collaboration EPs, <i>Castles</i> and <i>Castles II</i>. They were released on July 2, 2021, with video of past live performances of certain tracks from the EPs. In the fall of 2021, the estate released <i>Friends</i> and <i>High Fashion</i>, two previously unreleased EPs made in collaboration with Yunggoth and <a href="/wiki/Harry_Fraud" title="Harry Fraud">Harry Fraud</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> On May 20, 2022, the <i>Feelz</i> EP was re-released, with the videos for "feelz" and "life" also being released.<sup id="cite_ref-EDMDemons.com_2022_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDMDemons.com_2022-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> On December 2, 2022, the mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Live_Forever_(Lil_Peep_mixtape)" title="Live Forever (Lil Peep mixtape)">LIVE FOREVER</a></i> was re-released, with the music video for the mixtape's title track also being released.<sup id="cite_ref-Twitter_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Twitter-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 1, 2023, the estate released the collaboration with <a href="/wiki/ILoveMakonnen" title="ILoveMakonnen">ILoveMakonnen</a> "November" on all platforms. The estate also confirmed the duo's 2017 collaboration album <i>Diamonds</i> would be released on September 8, 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">Fashion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Peep&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Fashion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lil Peep had been into fashion since his teenage years, and during the last months of his life he modelled for <a href="/wiki/Vlone" class="mw-redirect" title="Vlone">Vlone</a> and was invited to and attended several fashion shows such as <a href="/wiki/Balmain_(fashion_house)" title="Balmain (fashion house)">Balmain</a> men's show at <a href="/wiki/Paris_Fashion_Week" title="Paris Fashion Week">Paris Fashion Week</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moncler" title="Moncler">Moncler</a> Gamme Bleu MFW Mens Spring Summer show in <a href="/wiki/Milan_Fashion_Week" title="Milan Fashion Week">Milan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:14222_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:14222-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:15_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:15-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Nico Amarca of <i>Hypebeast</i> said, "Even though Peep's brand of trendy sits on a far more niche spectrum than most modern-day tastemakers, something that largely attributed to his success. In a time where genuine individuality is becoming increasingly obsolete, Peep was the tattoo-covered, Manic Panic-hued mall rat the creative world needed to disrupt its ever-growing homogeny."<sup id="cite_ref-HYPEBEAST_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HYPEBEAST-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Rapper <a href="/wiki/Playboi_Carti" title="Playboi Carti">Playboi Carti</a> described Lil Peep as a "trendsetter".<sup id="cite_ref-HYPEBEAST_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HYPEBEAST-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His style has been described as evoking fashion styles associated with emo<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mall_goth" title="Mall goth">mall goth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vogue_Death_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vogue_Death-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> He often wore items including graffitied jackets, colored fur,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> and pink clothes.<sup id="cite_ref-Vogue_Death_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vogue_Death-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> He cited <a href="/wiki/Fat_Mike" title="Fat Mike">Fat Mike</a>, Marcelo Burlon and <a href="/wiki/The_Casualties" title="The Casualties">the Casualties</a> as style influences. In a 2017 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a></i>, he stated:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I never dress the same way for a week—I'll dress like a whole other person the next week. I like to get weird and mix things. Not necessarily draw on the streets, but mix darker, dirtier cultures with high class shit. And kind of fuse them together and see how they can become one. And I think that already happens when I put on any really elegant piece of clothing, because of the way I look. You expect me to dress like a fucking punk.<sup id="cite_ref-:14222_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:14222-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>In late 2018, it was announced that a Lil Peep clothing line was being created called "No Smoking" (stylized as "NO SMOK!NG") which was developed before Lil Peep's death.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style">Musical style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Peep&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Musical style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1134653256">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:#f9f9f9;display:flow-root}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096940132">.mw-parser-output .listen .side-box-text{line-height:1.1em}.mw-parser-output .listen-plain{border:none;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded{width:100%;margin:0;border-width:1px 0 0 0;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-header{padding:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded .listen-header{padding:2px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen-file-header{padding:4px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen .description{padding-top:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen .mw-tmh-player{max-width:100%}@media(max-width:719px){.mw-parser-output .listen{clear:both}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .listen:not(.listen-noimage){width:320px}.mw-parser-output .listen-left{overflow:visible;float:left}.mw-parser-output .listen-center{float:none;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}}</style><div class="side-box side-box-right listen noprint"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style>
<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-image"><figure class="mw-halign-center" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></span><figcaption></figcaption></figure></div>
<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><div class="haudio">
<div class="listen-file-header"><a href="/wiki/File:LP_MOBS.ogg" title="File:LP MOBS.ogg">"Move On Be Strong"</a></div>
<div><span typeof="mw:File"><span><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="232" style="width:232px;" data-durationhint="27" data-mwtitle="LP_MOBS.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/96/LP_MOBS.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (142 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/9/96/LP_MOBS.ogg/LP_MOBS.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" /></audio></span></span></div>
<div class="description">"Move On Be Strong" contains a sample from <a href="/wiki/Avenged_Sevenfold" title="Avenged Sevenfold">Avenged Sevenfold</a>. The song combines <a href="/wiki/Distortion_(music)" title="Distortion (music)">distorted</a> guitar <a href="/wiki/Riff" title="Riff">riffs</a> with abrasive <a href="/wiki/Trap_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Trap (music)">trap beats</a> and features Lil Peep's use of <a href="/wiki/Screaming_(music)" title="Screaming (music)">screaming vocals</a>.</div></div><hr /><div class="haudio">
<div class="listen-file-header"><a href="/wiki/File:LP_HB_Track_6.ogg" title="File:LP HB Track 6.ogg">"Cobain"</a></div>
<div><span typeof="mw:File"><span><audio id="mwe_player_1" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="232" style="width:232px;" data-durationhint="20" data-mwtitle="LP_HB_Track_6.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/32/LP_HB_Track_6.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (150 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/3/32/LP_HB_Track_6.ogg/LP_HB_Track_6.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" /></audio></span></span></div>
<div class="description">"Cobain" from his breakthrough mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Hellboy_(Lil_Peep_mixtape)" title="Hellboy (Lil Peep mixtape)">Hellboy</a></i> (2016) harbors downcast lyrics, and the title references <a href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)" title="Nirvana (band)">Nirvana</a> frontman <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain" title="Kurt Cobain">Kurt Cobain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Amorosi_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amorosi-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Lil Peep intones emotionally raw lines laced with hazy, narcotic <a href="/wiki/Melodies" class="mw-redirect" title="Melodies">melodies</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Deadpan" title="Deadpan">deadpan</a> voice.<sup id="cite_ref-Lal_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lal-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The song features poignant samples of "Bad News" by <a href="/wiki/Indie_folk" title="Indie folk">indie-folk</a> singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Owen_(musician)" title="Owen (musician)">Owen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lal_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lal-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div></div>
<div class="side-box-abovebelow"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing these files? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></div>
</div>
<p>Lil Peep was described as making <a href="/wiki/Lo-fi_music" title="Lo-fi music">lo-fi rap</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> being an "emo-trap heart throb"<sup id="cite_ref-Tiny_Mix_Tapes_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tiny_Mix_Tapes-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> and an "emo rapper".<sup id="cite_ref-AllMusic_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusic-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nme_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nme-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Music journalists often compared Lil Peep to singer-songwriter and guitarist <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain" title="Kurt Cobain">Kurt Cobain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Robles_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robles-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i> music critic <a href="/wiki/Jon_Caramanica" title="Jon Caramanica">Jon Caramanica</a> defined Peep as the <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain" title="Kurt Cobain">Kurt Cobain</a> of lo-fi rap, describing his music as gloomy and diabolically melodic.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Lil Peep himself encouraged the connection and persona in his musical and lyrical content, saying that he wanted to become the "New Kurt Cobain".<sup id="cite_ref-Robles_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robles-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> According to Angus Harrison from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, Lil Peep was "repurposing Kurt Cobain for bedroom diarists who are more used to rap than they are guitars."<sup id="cite_ref-Harrison_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harrison-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> described Lil Peep's music as a blend of <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> influences along with <a href="/wiki/Trap_music_(hip_hop)" class="mw-redirect" title="Trap music (hip hop)">trap</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dream_pop" title="Dream pop">dream pop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> His songs generally drew on the <a href="/wiki/Triple_metre" title="Triple metre">triple-time</a> <a href="/wiki/Hi-hats" class="mw-redirect" title="Hi-hats">hi-hats</a> of <a href="/wiki/Southern_rap" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern rap">Southern rap</a> and the angsty introspection of <a href="/wiki/Post-hardcore" title="Post-hardcore">post-hardcore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Harrison_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harrison-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> He combined elements of emo and <a href="/wiki/Pop_punk" class="mw-redirect" title="Pop punk">pop punk</a> into rap music, bringing a fresh take on the genre.<sup id="cite_ref-Tenreyro_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tenreyro-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> This resulted in him being described as the "future of emo" by Steven J. Horowitz of online magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(website)" title="Pitchfork (website)">Pitchfork</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tenreyro_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tenreyro-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a burgeoning artist, Lil Peep gained a significant amount of traction in the <a href="/wiki/Alternative_hip-hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Alternative hip-hop">alternative hip-hop</a> scene, establishing a better platform for himself to speak to fans about topics of his concern such as <a href="/wiki/Mental_health" title="Mental health">mental health</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bell_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bell-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> His lyrical themes include topics such as <a href="/wiki/Mood_disorder" title="Mood disorder">depression</a>, <a href="/wiki/Substance_abuse" title="Substance abuse">drug use</a>, past relationships, and <a href="/wiki/Suicidal_thoughts" class="mw-redirect" title="Suicidal thoughts">suicidal thoughts</a> and meshes together third-wave emo, alternative rock, pop-punk and dream pop with trap music and hip-hop.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> A close friend and the executive producer of <i>Come Over When You're Sober, Pt. 1</i> said that Peep "wanted to give a voice to people that suffer from anxiety and depression, people who have been abused, bullied, and the people who were misunderstood like him. He had demons of his own and he faced those demons by creating music."<sup id="cite_ref-For_Lil_Peep_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-For_Lil_Peep-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Peep&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lil Peep was candid about struggles with his sexuality, <a href="/wiki/Clinical_depression" class="mw-redirect" title="Clinical depression">depression</a>, heartbreak, and drug use.<sup id="cite_ref-Brandle_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brandle-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Lil Peep came out as <a href="/wiki/Bisexual" class="mw-redirect" title="Bisexual">bisexual</a> in a Twitter post on August 8, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tenreyro_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tenreyro-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> He took to Twitter to open up about this aspect of his personal life to his fans.<sup id="cite_ref-Bell_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bell-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Lil Peep simply stated, "yes i'm bi sexual."<sup id="cite_ref-Tenreyro_103-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tenreyro-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> After coming out as bisexual, he would regularly confront <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">homophobes</a> on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> He was also known collaborators with <a href="/wiki/ILoveMakonnen" title="ILoveMakonnen">iLoveMakonnen</a>, an openly gay recording artist whose music also blurs the line between rap and rock.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lil Peep came out around the time he and actress and singer <a href="/wiki/Bella_Thorne" title="Bella Thorne">Bella Thorne</a> began dating in September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Tenreyro_103-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tenreyro-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after the release of his debut studio album, the two were spotted kissing. They briefly dated, before Thorne became involved with rapper <a href="/wiki/Mod_Sun" title="Mod Sun">Mod Sun</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tenreyro_103-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tenreyro-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> While on the <a href="/wiki/Come_Over_When_You%27re_Sober,_Pt._1" title="Come Over When You&#39;re Sober, Pt. 1">Come Over When You're Sober tour</a>, Lil Peep had met and started dating Instagram influencer Arzaylea Rodriguez around the time of his death in November.<sup id="cite_ref-Peisner_Peisner_2019_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peisner_Peisner_2019-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lil Peep actively talked about his issues with depression, <a href="/wiki/Anxiety" title="Anxiety">anxiety</a> and <a href="/wiki/Substance_abuse" title="Substance abuse">substance abuse</a> and stated that he had <a href="/wiki/Bipolar_disorder" title="Bipolar disorder">bipolar disorder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:22_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:22-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Alongside drug use, Lil Peep struggled with <a href="/wiki/Suicidal_ideation" title="Suicidal ideation">suicidal impulses</a> that date back to his adolescent years.<sup id="cite_ref-Blend_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blend-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> On the track "OMFG" from his breakthrough mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Hellboy_(Lil_Peep_mixtape)" title="Hellboy (Lil Peep mixtape)">Hellboy</a></i>, Lil Peep talked about wanting to kill himself.<sup id="cite_ref-Horowitz_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horowitz-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> During an interview, he was asked if he was suicidal. Lil Peep replied, "Yeah, it is serious. I suffer from depression and some days I wake up and I'm like, Fuck, I wish I didn't wake up. That was part of why I moved to California, trying to get away from the place that was doing that to me, and the people I was around."<sup id="cite_ref-Horowitz_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horowitz-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> He continued, "I realized it was just myself—it's a <a href="/wiki/Chemical_imbalance" class="mw-redirect" title="Chemical imbalance">chemical imbalance</a> in my brain. Some days I'll be very down and out, but you won't be able to tell, really, because I don't express that side of myself on social media. That's the side of myself that I express through music. That's my channel for letting all that shit out."<sup id="cite_ref-Horowitz_111-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horowitz-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> He claims the frankness with which he spoke about difficulties in his life led to an intense connection with his fans through his music. In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>, Lil Peep stated, "They tell me that it saved their lives. They say that I stopped them from committing suicide, which is a beautiful thing. ... It's great for me to hear. It helps. It boosts me, because music saved my life as well."<sup id="cite_ref-Blend_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blend-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lil Peep was not medicated for depression. While those around him insisted, he did not want to, and opted to instead <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">smoke cannabis</a> and consume whichever other drugs came his way.<sup id="cite_ref-Horowitz_111-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horowitz-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In his final interview before his death with Zane Lowe, Peep confessed that his depression was getting worse saying "Things just get worse. Things already get worse and worse and worse every day."<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Lil Peep regularly referenced <a href="/wiki/Cocaine_addiction" class="mw-redirect" title="Cocaine addiction">addictions to cocaine</a>, <a href="/wiki/MDMA" title="MDMA">ecstasy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alprazolam" title="Alprazolam">Xanax</a> in his lyrics and posts on social media,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> where he described himself as a "productive junkie" and advised his audience to avoid drug use.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the time of his death, Lil Peep was residing in <a href="/wiki/Portobello_Road" title="Portobello Road">Portobello Road</a>, London, with his friend and close collaborator Bexey,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:22_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:22-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and Smokeasac. The move was provoked by Peep's need to escape his circumstances and his then-collective GothBoiClique.<sup id="cite_ref-:24_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:24-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Peep&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On November 15, 2017, Lil Peep was found dead on his tour bus when his manager went to check on him in preparation for that night's performance at a <a href="/wiki/Tucson,_Arizona" title="Tucson, Arizona">Tucson, Arizona</a>, venue.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Foul play was not suspected,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> with his death believed to be from an overdose.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> In a series of <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> posts in the hours leading up to his death, Lil Peep claimed to have ingested <a href="/wiki/Psilocybin_mushrooms" class="mw-redirect" title="Psilocybin mushrooms">psilocybin mushrooms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_concentrate" title="Cannabis concentrate">cannabis concentrate</a>. In another, he claimed to have consumed six <a href="/wiki/Alprazolam" title="Alprazolam">Xanax</a> pills following a video depicting his attempts to drop an unidentified pill into his mouth several times before successfully swallowing one and shaking a full prescription bottle. A subsequent post was captioned, "When I die, you'll love me."<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> In the days after his death, a police report revealed that Lil Peep had taken a nap around 5:45&#160;p.m. before the concert. His manager checked on him twice and found him sleeping and breathing fine, but was unable to wake him. When the manager checked on Lil Peep a third time, he was unresponsive and not breathing. Lil Peep's manager performed <a href="/wiki/Cardiopulmonary_resuscitation" title="Cardiopulmonary resuscitation">CPR</a> before medics arrived, though he was pronounced dead at the scene.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 8, <a href="/wiki/Pima_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Pima County">Pima County</a>'s Office of the Medical Examiner certified his cause of death as an accidental overdose from the powerful pain medication <a href="/wiki/Fentanyl" title="Fentanyl">fentanyl</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine" title="Benzodiazepine">benzodiazepine</a> <a href="/wiki/Alprazolam" title="Alprazolam">Xanax</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Sedative" title="Sedative">sedative</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-deathofficial_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deathofficial-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Toxicology tests were also positive for <a href="/wiki/Cannabis" title="Cannabis">cannabis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a> and the painkiller <a href="/wiki/Tramadol" title="Tramadol">Tramadol</a>. Urine tests also showed the presence of multiple powerful <a href="/wiki/Opioid" title="Opioid">opioids</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Hydrocodone" title="Hydrocodone">hydrocodone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hydromorphone" title="Hydromorphone">hydromorphone</a> (marketed under the brand name Dilaudid), <a href="/wiki/Oxycodone" title="Oxycodone">oxycodone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oxymorphone" title="Oxymorphone">oxymorphone</a>. There was no alcohol in his system.<sup id="cite_ref-people_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-people-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wrongful_death_lawsuit">Wrongful death lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Peep&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Wrongful death lawsuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The rapper's mother Liza Womack filed <a href="/wiki/Wrongful_death_claim#United_States" title="Wrongful death claim">wrongful death charges</a> against Lil Peep's management <a href="/wiki/FAE_grp" title="FAE grp">FAE grp</a> in 2019, accusing them of "negligence and other breaches of contract which, the lawsuit alleges, contributed to his death in 2017 of an accidental drug overdose." Among the claims in the lawsuit are that FAE was complicit in providing access to "illegal drugs" and "prescription medications", and that the company knowingly allowed drug use to take place during the rapper's tour "despite being aware of his addiction". At one point, the lawsuit charges that FAE encouraged the star to take drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-CMU_2019_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMU_2019-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> In a responding statement, FAE expressed disappointment in the lawsuit:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"Lil Peep's death from an accidental drug overdose was a terrible tragedy. However, the claim that First Access Entertainment, any of its employees, or Chase Ortega, or anyone else under our auspices, was somehow responsible for, complicit in, or contributed to his death is categorically untrue. In fact, we consistently encouraged Peep to stop abusing drugs and to distance himself from the negative influence of the drug users and enablers with whom he chose to associate."<sup id="cite_ref-CMU_2019_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMU_2019-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>FAE formally filed court documents at the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County_Superior_Court" title="Los Angeles County Superior Court">Los Angeles County Superior Court</a> on December 23, 2019, to dispute all claims, including claims of negligence, breach of contract, "and wrongful death". Stennett told <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> that "[she] felt very protective of Lil Peep from day one." In later documents and court filings, the company said that their work with Lil Peep was an "arm's length business arrangement", something disputed by the rapper's mother.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite court filings, FAE supported the release of Peep's first <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/posthumous" class="extiw" title="wikt:posthumous">posthumous</a> album <i><a href="/wiki/Come_Over_When_You%27re_Sober,_Pt._2" title="Come Over When You&#39;re Sober, Pt. 2">Come Over When You're Sober, Pt. 2</a></i> (2018), which reached number four on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, a career-best for the rapper.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> At the start of 2020, the company released statements about their belief that they had no contractual responsibility for Lil Peep's personal life, and that a ruling to suggest so would damage management businesses, "Imposing a duty on FAE Ltd. or FAE LLC to prevent [Lil Peep's] drug overdose would extend the boundaries of legal obligations far beyond any precedent, and far beyond the contractual obligations and reasonable expectations of parties doing business. It would convert businesses engaged in the music and entertainment industries into full-time babysitters for artists. That clearly was not the parties' intent upon entering 'the JVA [(joint-venture agreement)].'"<sup id="cite_ref-MBW_JVAs_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MBW_JVAs-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After four years in the court system, the lawsuit was settled in February 2023 before going to trial.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> While the majority of the terms of the settlement were not made public, it was revealed that moving forward that Peep's entire catalog of music would move from FAE to be handled under the care of his surviving family.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tributes">Tributes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Peep&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tributes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Numerous artists in the music industry paid tribute to Lil Peep following his death, including <a href="/wiki/Diplo" title="Diplo">Diplo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Post_Malone" title="Post Malone">Post Malone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pete_Wentz" title="Pete Wentz">Pete Wentz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshmello" title="Marshmello">Marshmello</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ronson" title="Mark Ronson">Mark Ronson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zane_Lowe" title="Zane Lowe">Zane Lowe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Smith_(singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sam Smith (singer)">Sam Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bella_Thorne" title="Bella Thorne">Bella Thorne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trippie_Redd" title="Trippie Redd">Trippie Redd</a>, <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Nast" title="ASAP Nast">A$AP Nast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rich_Brian" title="Rich Brian">Rich Brian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Playboi_Carti" title="Playboi Carti">Playboi Carti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ugly_God" title="Ugly God">Ugly God</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Uzi_Vert" title="Lil Uzi Vert">Lil Uzi Vert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Xan" title="Lil Xan">Lil Xan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ty_Dolla_Sign" title="Ty Dolla Sign">Ty Dolla Sign</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Pump" title="Lil Pump">Lil Pump</a>, <a href="/wiki/XXXTentacion" title="XXXTentacion">XXXTentacion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dua_Lipa" title="Dua Lipa">Dua Lipa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/El-P" title="El-P">El-P</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:7_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jon_Caramanica" title="Jon Caramanica">Jon Caramanica</a>, a music critic for <i>The New York Times</i>, held a special remembrance podcast episode to honor Peep following his death which was released on November 22, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Good_Charlotte" title="Good Charlotte">Good Charlotte</a> also honored Lil Peep, releasing a cover of "Awful Things", which was shown at his memorial in Long Beach, New York on December 2, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Three_Days_Grace" title="Three Days Grace">Three Days Grace</a> paid tribute by posting a video on Instagram and Twitter of a remix of Peep's song "Witchblades" featuring <a href="/wiki/Lil_Tracy" title="Lil Tracy">Lil Tracy</a>. The remixed song's beat was a slowed down instrumental track of the band's song "The Real You". Lil Peep would be mentioned by <a href="/wiki/Juicy_J" title="Juicy J">Juicy J</a> (who had collaborated with him before his death) on <a href="/wiki/Rae_Sremmurd" title="Rae Sremmurd">Rae Sremmurd</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Powerglide_(song)" title="Powerglide (song)">Powerglide</a>". Lil Peep was also honored during the <a href="/wiki/60th_Annual_Grammy_Awards#In_Memoriam" title="60th Annual Grammy Awards">60th Grammy Awards</a>. On June 19, 2018, <a href="/wiki/Juice_Wrld" title="Juice Wrld">Juice Wrld</a> released a two-song EP titled <i>Too Soon..</i> dedicated to him and XXXTentacion, the latter being <a href="/wiki/Killing_of_XXXTentacion" class="mw-redirect" title="Killing of XXXTentacion">killed in June 2018</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/The_1975" title="The 1975">The 1975</a> track, "<a href="/wiki/Love_It_If_We_Made_It" title="Love It If We Made It">Love It If We Made It</a>", there is a lyric that gives a tribute to Lil Peep: "Rest in peace Lil Peep, The poetry is in the streets".<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> In the song "Glass House" by <a href="/wiki/Machine_Gun_Kelly_(musician)" title="Machine Gun Kelly (musician)">Machine Gun Kelly</a>, which pays tribute to many deceased artists, Lil Peep is mentioned in the lines: "Wish Lil Peep and me had met, but I can't get that back". Fellow emo rapper XXXTentacion shared similar sentiments, saying that if he and Lil Peep had known each other better that they would have been good friends.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> XXXTentacion recorded a verse for a song in tribute to Lil Peep prior to his own murder, which was later turned into the posthumous collaboration "<a href="/wiki/Falling_Down_(Lil_Peep_and_XXXTentacion_song)" title="Falling Down (Lil Peep and XXXTentacion song)">Falling Down</a>". <a href="/wiki/Grimes" title="Grimes">Grimes</a> stated that she wrote the song "<a href="/wiki/Delete_Forever" title="Delete Forever">Delete Forever</a>" on the night of Lil Peep's death, with the lyrics being inspired by substance abuse.<sup id="cite_ref-Shaffer_Shaffer_2020_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shaffer_Shaffer_2020-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lil Peep was cremated at <a href="/wiki/Huntington_Station,_New_York" title="Huntington Station, New York">Huntington Station, New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> On December 2, 2017, friends, family and fans paid their respects to Lil Peep at his memorial in <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach,_New_York" title="Long Beach, New York">Long Beach, New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> A memorial was also held in London on the same day that a large picture of Lil Peep was projected onto the side of the <a href="/wiki/Houses_of_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Houses of parliament">Houses of Parliament</a> in <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">central London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy_and_influence">Legacy and influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Peep&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Legacy and influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:LilPeep-Hellboy_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/LilPeep-Hellboy_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-LilPeep-Hellboy_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="226" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/LilPeep-Hellboy_%28cropped%29.jpg/331px-LilPeep-Hellboy_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/LilPeep-Hellboy_%28cropped%29.jpg/441px-LilPeep-Hellboy_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="471" data-file-height="483" /></a><figcaption>Before he died of an accidental <a href="/wiki/Drug_overdose" title="Drug overdose">overdose</a> on November 15, 2017, in <a href="/wiki/Tucson,_Arizona" title="Tucson, Arizona">Tucson</a>, Lil Peep was believed to be on track in taking <a href="/wiki/SoundCloud_rap" class="mw-redirect" title="SoundCloud rap">SoundCloud rap</a> into the pop mainstream.<sup id="cite_ref-End_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-End-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup></figcaption></figure><p>Before dying at the age of 21, Lil Peep came to be an inspiration to outcasts and <a href="/wiki/Youth_subculture" title="Youth subculture">youth subcultures</a> drawn together by the internet.<sup id="cite_ref-Hypebeast_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hypebeast-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> He earned legions of fans in a short time from both <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emo_Subculture" class="mw-redirect" title="Emo Subculture">emo</a> subcultures.<sup id="cite_ref-Kornhaber_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kornhaber-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Although he did not claim so himself, he is widely considered to have made a style of music that has been since regarded "emo rap".<sup id="cite_ref-Eloise_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eloise-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Harrison_101-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harrison-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> He has been credited as the leading figure of the mid–late 2010s <a href="/wiki/Emo_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Emo music">emo music</a> scene<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> and is commonly cited as an inspiration for upcoming emo rappers.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>At the time of Lil Peep's death, he was on the cusp of something significant. Three months earlier, he'd released <i><a href="/wiki/Come_Over_When_You%27re_Sober,_Pt._1" title="Come Over When You&#39;re Sober, Pt. 1">Come Over When You're Sober, Pt. 1</a></i>, the album that took the skeleton sound he'd developed in his bedroom — emo sentimentality, thunderous hip-hop underbelly, rock-star insouciance — and thickened it up. His mixtapes <i><a href="/wiki/Hellboy_(Lil_Peep_mixtape)" title="Hellboy (Lil Peep mixtape)">Hellboy</a></i> and <i>Crybaby</i>, released on SoundCloud, were on the front lines of hip-hop's open-eared engagement with other genres, as well as documents of the ways emo and pop-punk had begun to make room for hip-hop. He was at the musical vanguard and, covered in a symphony of tattoos, an emerging fashion icon as well. – <i>New York Times</i> music critic <a href="/wiki/Jon_Caramanica" title="Jon Caramanica">Jon Caramanica</a><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>In 2017, <i><a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(website)" title="Pitchfork (website)">Pitchfork</a></i> hailed Lil Peep as "the future of emo".<sup id="cite_ref-Tenreyro_103-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tenreyro-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Regarding his death, in January 2018, <a href="/wiki/John_Jeremiah_Sullivan" title="John Jeremiah Sullivan">John Jeremiah Sullivan</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a></i> wrote, "When Lil Peep died late last year, he left behind an outsized legacy."<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> journalist Elias Leight concurred similarly and wrote that Lil Peep's "rise to stardom was powered by relentless drive."<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> A profile on his artistry was written by <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> editor Steven Horowitz.<sup id="cite_ref-Tenreyro_103-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tenreyro-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The lengthy article resulted in an influx of <a href="/wiki/Think_piece" class="mw-redirect" title="Think piece">think pieces</a> centered around Lil Peep amongst writers, with music publications such as <i><a href="/wiki/Noisey" class="mw-redirect" title="Noisey">Noisey</a></i> discussing his role within the broader emo genre.
