Though it allowed Peep to gather attention from a wide audience beyond his SoundCloud base, the piece polarized readers, some of whom protested applying the "future of emo" label to the young rapper in the headline.<sup id="cite_ref-Eloise_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eloise-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tenreyro_103-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tenreyro-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> However, Lil Peep has since become regarded being an integral part of a "<a href="/wiki/Emo_revival" title="Emo revival">post-emo revival</a> style of <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-:17_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:17-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:18_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:18-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:19_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:19-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:20_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:20-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> and had been described as "arguably the biggest emo icon of the past few years"<sup id="cite_ref-:21_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:21-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The death of Lil Peep left an impact on several of his musical contemporaries.<sup id="cite_ref-Valentine_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Valentine-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lil_Uzi_Vert" title="Lil Uzi Vert">Lil Uzi Vert</a> offered tribute by sharing on Twitter an edited version of one of the final photos Lil Peep had shared online.<sup id="cite_ref-Valentine_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Valentine-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> The news of Lil Peep's tragic passing greatly affected Lil Uzi Vert, who shortly tweeted, "We would love 2 stop ..... but do you really care cause we been on <a href="/wiki/Xanax" class="mw-redirect" title="Xanax">xanax</a> all fucking year. [...] Rip buddy I 100% understand and I don't fault u."<sup id="cite_ref-Valentine_154-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Valentine-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> The prescription pills <a href="/wiki/Xanax" class="mw-redirect" title="Xanax">Xanax</a> has since become an epidemic in the hip hop realm, particularly among the current SoundCloud generation.<sup id="cite_ref-Newstead_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newstead-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/SoundCloud_rap" class="mw-redirect" title="SoundCloud rap">SoundCloud rap</a> scene Lil Peep originated from is notorious for its drug use, with artists often abusing prescription pills such as Xanax which have since become a go-to <a href="/wiki/Metaphor" title="Metaphor">metaphor</a> in their lyrics.<sup id="cite_ref-Brown,_August_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown,_August-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> In an assessment of the reactions, many were hopeful Lil Peep's death has served as a wake-up call for the community regarding <a href="/wiki/Drug_abuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Drug abuse">drug abuse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Newstead_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newstead-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> After offering their thoughts, Lil Uzi Vert indicated they were looking to do something for themselves in response to Lil Peep's untimely passing.<sup id="cite_ref-Newstead_155-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newstead-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Lil Uzi Vert also seemed to make attempts to <a href="/wiki/Detox" class="mw-redirect" title="Detox">detox</a>, and the following Thursday tweeted an update saying they were <a href="/wiki/Sobriety" title="Sobriety">sober</a> for the day and already shaking.<sup id="cite_ref-Valentine_154-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Valentine-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the years following his death, Lil Peep became influential on the development of the <a href="/wiki/E-girls_and_e-boys" title="E-girls and e-boys">e-girls and e-boys</a> subculture.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to calling him "the future of emo", <i><a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(website)" title="Pitchfork (website)">Pitchfork</a></i> also posited that Lil Peep's willingness to be vulnerable was an antidote to the toxic attitude towards women, which in the past has been a core element of hip-hop culture and its <a href="/wiki/Rap-rock" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap-rock">rap-rock</a> variant.<sup id="cite_ref-Weiss_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weiss-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> According to fellow GothBoiClique member, Fish Narc, Lil Peep explicitly rejected contemporary SoundCloud rapper XXXTentacion for his alleged history of <a href="/wiki/XXXTentacion#Legal_issues" title="XXXTentacion">violence against his ex-girlfriend</a>, spending time and money removing XXXTentacion's songs from his <a href="/wiki/Spotify" title="Spotify">Spotify</a> playlists.<sup id="cite_ref-Daramola_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daramola-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> On the contrary, rapper Fat Nick, a mutual friend of Lil Peep and XXXTentacion, said on Twitter that right before Peep died, he and Peep had a conversation about XXXTentacion and had planned to meet up with him, and that XXXTentacion was "super happy about it".<sup id="cite_ref-hotnewhiphop.com_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hotnewhiphop.com-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Fat Nick also spoke about the matter on an Instagram <a href="/wiki/Livestream" class="mw-redirect" title="Livestream">livestream</a>, where he dismissed the claims from Fish Narc and others about tension between XXXTentacion and Lil Peep, and confirmed that Lil Peep wanted to meet XXXTentacion once he was off tour. In the livestream, he also implied that members of GothBoiClique were responsible for Lil Peep's death, saying, "Some of y'all are siding with the people that took advantage of Peep. I don't get it... That's crazy. Y'all say shit about fucking X, but you're not saying shit about the people that killed [Lil Peep]... The people that gave him fentanyl. Y'all don't say shit to them."<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> After this, Fish Narc faced criticism for his initial statement condemning the song. Fish Narc responded on Twitter, "I feel that people think I am trying to insult X. But really I wish him rest. I protest a posthumous collab between unaffiliated artists", and clarified that he did not wish to attack XXXTentacion and that his comments were, "how I interpreted what Peep told me as a friend."<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> When the posthumous 2018 single, "<a href="/wiki/Falling_Down_(Lil_Peep_and_XXXTentacion_song)" title="Falling Down (Lil Peep and XXXTentacion song)">Falling Down</a>", was created without Lil Peep's consent, uniting the two deceased rappers, some Lil Peep fans and some of Lil Peep's friends opposed the retroactive inclusion of XXXTentacion. Some surviving band members posted a story onto <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> disavowing the collaboration and imploring others not to listen to it.<sup id="cite_ref-Daramola_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daramola-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Following his death, <i><a href="/wiki/Mic_(media_company)" title="Mic (media company)">Mic</a></i> bemoaned: "Sadly, Peep had barely just begun bringing emo into the future with a message that many of his less woman-friendly influences, like <a href="/wiki/Brand_New_(band)" title="Brand New (band)">Brand New</a>, have failed to put forward." He continued saying, "For a 'crybaby' who left this world so young, Peep inspired a lot of people to keep going."<sup id="cite_ref-Weiss_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weiss-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The day after hearing news of his death, rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_B" title="Lil B">Lil B</a> paid tribute through a tweet. He wrote, "I remember Lil peep telling me he is against the <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abuse" title="Sexual abuse">sexual abuse</a> of women and people in the music industry<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... I will continue to push his vision."<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Achievements">Achievements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Peep&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Achievements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Having arisen from SoundCloud scene, Lil Peep was a large presence on social media and came to be revered online.<sup id="cite_ref-Garland_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garland-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Harrison_101-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harrison-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> He attracted a <a href="/wiki/Cult_following" title="Cult following">cult following</a> through the songs he released and their emotional, downtrodden lyrics.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Associated_Press_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Associated_Press-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Lil Peep also enjoyed the draw of his <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> channel, where several millions of views were generated by his music videos for "Awful Things", "<a href="/wiki/Benz_Truck" class="mw-redirect" title="Benz Truck">Benz Truck</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Brightside" class="mw-redirect" title="The Brightside">The Brightside</a>" among others.<sup id="cite_ref-Brandle_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brandle-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Atlantic" title="The Atlantic">The Atlantic</a></i>, "If you were going to bet on the young musicians most likely to soon be superstars, until yesterday, a lot of smart money would have been on Lil Peep."<sup id="cite_ref-Kornhaber_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kornhaber-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Lil Peep had laid before him a promising career, which had been on the rise since 2015 thanks to a series of tracks, <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EPs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtapes</a> released on SoundCloud.<sup id="cite_ref-Brandle_104-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brandle-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> After being around for a little more than a year, Lil Peep had already managed to amass millions of hits on YouTube and SoundCloud.<sup id="cite_ref-Garland_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garland-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> A year after posting his first song, Lil Peep attracted 82,000 followers on SoundCloud and 112,000 followers on <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Horowitz_111-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horowitz-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The burgeoning rapper had generated millions of online <a href="/wiki/Streaming_media" title="Streaming media">streams</a> before releasing his debut album <i>Come Over When You're Sober Pt. 1</i> in August 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Garrett_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garrett-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Despite being involved with <a href="/wiki/GothBoiClique" title="GothBoiClique">GothBoiClique</a> for the shortest amount of time, Lil Peep became the first member of the group to be paid serious critical attention as well as tour internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-Garland_163-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garland-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Due in part to his divisive nature, Lil Peep made his way onto <i>Pitchfork</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> <i>"</i>Best Songs of the Year" list and completed a largely sold-out tour of Russia and Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Garland_163-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garland-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Peep&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Peep&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
